purposes connected therewith. (Unemployment Insurance
(Agreement).)

Housing Act (Northern Ireland),1923,asamended by subsequent
enactments . (Housing .)

1922 to 1925,by increasingthe amount of loanswhich may be
guaranteed under the said Acts and extending the period for
givingguaranteesthereunder,and to authorisethe Ministryof
Finance to contribute towards the interest on certain loans
guaranteedunder the saidActs. (Loans Guarantee.)

the public servicestransferred to the Government of Northern
Irelandby virtueof the Ireland (Confirmationof Agreement )

CHAPTER 1 .
An Act to confirm and give effectto an agreement
made between the Treasury ofthe United King-
dom and the Ministry of Finance for Northern
Ireland with a view to assimilating the burdens
on the Exchequers of the United Kingdom and
Northern Ireland with respectto unemployment
insurance ,and for purposes connected therewith .
[23rd March , 1926.]
WHEREAS ,withaviewtoassimilatingtheburdensExchequer ofthe Kingdom and the
Exchequer ofNorthernIreland,perhead ofpopulation,
in respectof unemployment insurance, the Treasuryof
the United Kingdom and the Ministry of Finance for
Northern Ireland have entered into the agreement set
forth in the schedule to thisAct , and it is expedient
that the said agreement should be confirmed and that
provision should be made for or with respect to the
payment of such sums as may be payable out of or into
the Exchequer of Northern Ireland thereunder, and
for other matters arisingin relationto the Northern
Irish unemployment fund by reason of the said
agreement :
A.D 1926 .

Be it therefore enacted by the King's most
Excellent Majesty, and the Senate and the House of
Commons of Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament
assembled,and by the authorityofthesame ,asfollows:-
1. The agreement set forth in the schedule to this
Act (inthisAct referredto as "thescheduledagreement ")
ishereby confirmed and shallhave effectas ifenacted
in this Act .
2. Any sums certifiedby the Joint Exchequer
Board to be payable under the scheduled agreement
by the Exchequer of Northern Irelandto the Exchequer
ofthe United Kingdom shallbe charged on and paid out
of the Consolidated Fund of Northern Ireland or the
growing produce thereof.
3.-(1) There shall, in respect of each financial
year to which the scheduled agreement applies, be paid
out of moneys provided by the Parliament of Northern
Ireland to the Northern Irish unemployment fund
(in thisAct referredto as " the unemployment fund "),
inadditionto any othercontributionspayableintothe
unemployment fund by the Exchequer of Northern
Ireland,suchamount (ifany)asmay be certifiedby the
Ministry of Finance to be equal to the equalisation
payment , as defined in and determined in accordance
with the scheduled agreement, for such financialyear(which amount is in this Act referred to as " the
Exchequer equalisationgrant ").
(2) Payments may be made out of moneys pro-
vided as aforesaidto the unemployment fund on account
of the Exchequer equalisationgrant in such manner
and at such times as may be prescribedunder thisAct .
4.-(1) The unemployment fund shall comprise
a suspense account and a current account .
(2) The suspense account of the unemployment
fund shallshow so much of the liabilityof that fund, in
respectof advances repayableto the Exchequer of
Northern Ireland, as isequalto the sum which would
have been requiredto be paid into that fund as at the
thirtiethday of September , nineteen hundred and
twenty-five, in order to bring it into a stateof parity

SCHEDULE .
Short title.
AGREEMENT MADE BETWEEN THE TREASURY AND THE MINISTRY
OF FINANCE FOR NORTHERN IRELAND WITH A VIEW TO ASSIMIL-
ATING THE BURDENS ON THE EXCHEQUER OF THE UNITED
KINGDOM AND ON THE EXCHEQUER OF NORTHERN IRELAND IN
RESPECT OF UNEMPLOYMENT INSURANCE .
The Treasury and the Ministryof Finance forNorthern Ireland,
with a view to assimilatingthe burdens on the Exchequer of the
United Kingdom and the Exchequer of Northern Ireland,per head of
populations,inrespectof unemployment insurance,have enteredinto
the followingagreement :
1. There shallin respectof each financialyear be ascertained
the surplusor deficiencyof the unemployment funds of Great Britain
and Northern Ireland,and the amount requiredto be paid intothe
thefund which is,as compared with the otherfund,inthe lessfavour-
ableposition,inorderto bringthefundsintoa stateofparityinrespect
of that year,on the basisof the insuredpopulationsof Great Britain
and Northern Ireland, respectively.
The fund which isin the lessfavourablepositionishereinafter
referredto as "the poorerfund."
The payment requiredto be made intothe poorerfund in order
tobringitintosuch a stateofparityasaforesaidishereinafterreferred
to as " the equalisationpayment ."

## Page 11

[16 GEO .5.] 5Unemployment Insurance [Ch .1.]
(Agreement)Act
(NorthernIreland),1926.
The surplusor deficiencyof an unemployment fund in respect
of any financialyear shallbe ascertainedby comparing the receipts
of the fund on income account in that year,excludingany sums paid
intothefundduringtheyearon accountoftheequalisationpayment
under thisagreementor by way of advancesfrom the Exchequer,
with the expenditurefrom the fund on income accountin the year,
includingthe amount paidforthatyear by way ofintereston advances
from the Exchequer made to that fund in that or any previousyear
and forthe time being outstanding,but excludingany sums paid by
way of repayment of advances from the Exchequer .
2. If as respectsany year thereispaid intothe poorerfund by
way of grant from the Exchequer of the country to which that fund
belongs,inadditionto any othercontributionspayable intothat fund
from thatExchequer,an amount equalto theequalisationpayment,
thereshallbe paidintothatExchequer from the Exchequer oftheother
country,a contributioncalculatedin manner hereinafterappearing.
3. The contribution from one Exchequer to the other in respect
of a financialyearshallbe a sum equaltothree-fourthsofsuchsum
as may be requiredto equaliseper head of the populationof the
respectivecountriesthepayments from theExchequersoftherespective
countriesintotheirrespectiveunemployment funds in respectof that
year (excludingany payments on account of advances from those
Exchequers to theirrespectiveunemployment funds but including,
inthecaseofthecountryto which thepoorerfund belongs,theamount
of the equalisationpayment ).
4. There may be paid from time to time from the Exchequer
of the country to which an unemployment fund belongs into that
fund sums on account of the equalisationpayment which may ulti-
matelybe foundtobe due tothatfund,and whereany suchpayment
on account ismade from an Exchequer, thereshallbe paid to that
Exchequer from the Exchequer ofthe othercountryon accountofthe
contributionwhich may ultimatelybe found to be due such sum as
the Joint Exchequer Board may determineto be proper.
5. If at any time the classesof personsinsured, the ratesof
contribution or the rates or conditions of benefit differ in the two
countries,thereshallbe made such adjustmentsin the amount of the
equalisationpayment and the contributionfrom one Exchequer to
the otheras the Joint Exchequer Board ,afte. consultingthe Govern-
ment Actuary,considerjust.
6.-(1)If at any time the proportionof the receiptsof an
unemployment fund which may be appliedas an appropriationin aid
of moneys provided by Parliamentforthe purpose of administrative
expenses differsin the two countries, and by reason thereofthe
proportion of the receiptsso applied in one country exceeds the
amount whichmighthave beensoappliediftheproportionshad been
thesame ,theamount ofsuchexcessshall,forthepurposeofdetermining
thesurplusor deficiencyof thatfund,not be treatedas expenditure
from that fund .
A.D. 1926,

## Page 12

6 [16 GEO .5.][Ch .1.] Unemployment Insurance
A.D. 1926
(Agreement)Act
(NorthernIreland), 1926.
(2) The sums paid intoar unemployment fund on accountofthe
equalisationpayment under thisagreement shallnot be treatedas
receiptsof thefund indeterminingthe amount which may be paid
asan appropriationinaidofmoneys providedby Parliamentforthe
purposeofadministrativeexpenses.
7. Any questionarisingunder thisagreement as to the amount
of any equalisationpayment or of a contributionfrom one Exchequer
to the other,or otherwise,shallbe determined by the JointExchequer
Board , whose decision shall be final.
8. For thepurposesofthisagreement in relationto any financial
year-
(a) the populationsof Great Britainand Northern Ireland
respectivelyshallbe deemed to be such as may be certified
by the Registrar-General, after consultationwith the
Registrar-GeneralforScotland,and by the Registrar-General
ofNorthern Ireland,respectively,to be in theiropinion the
populationon thethirtiethday ofJune inthatyear:
(b) the expression" insuredpopulation" means the number
of persons certifiedby the Ministerof Labour and the
Ministryof Labour forNorthern Ireland,respectively,with
the concurrenceof the Government Actuary as being in
their opinion the number of persons insured under the
enactments relatingto unemployment insurancein Great
Britainand Northern Ireland,respectively,on the thirtieth
day of June in that year (excludingpersonsinsuredunder
any specialscheme made under any of those enactments).
9. This agreement shallnot come intooperationuntilconfirmed
by Acts of the Parliaments of the United Kingdom and Northern
Ireland, but upon being so confirmed shallapply as from the first
day ofOctober,nineteenhundred and twenty-five,untilthe thirty-first
day ofMarch ,nineteenhundred and thirty.
10.For the purposesof thisagreement, the periodfrom the
firstday of October,nineteenhundred and twenty-five,to the thirty-
firstday of March ,nineteenhundred and twenty-six,shallbe deemed
tobe a financialyear ;and inrelationto thatperiodtheperiodfrom the
firstday ofApriltothethirtiethday ofSeptember,nineteenhundred
and twenty-five,shallbedeemed tobe a previousyear,and references
inparagraphs(a)and (b)ofArticle8 ofthisagreementtothethirtieth
day ofJune ina yearshallbe construedasreferencesto thethirtieth
day of June ,nineteenhundred and twenty-five.
(Signed)]
H. M. POLLOCK .

section one of the Housing Act (Northern

enactments . 30th March , 1926 .

and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same , as follows:-
A.D. 1926 .

Ireland),1923,as amended by the Housing Acts Amend-

nineteenhundred and twenty -seven."

localauthorityor in a ruraldistrictimmediately before

orcouncil,by whom the resolutionwas adopted,expressly
so determine(but not otherwise),have effectsoastoapply
to houses in respectof whose constructionthe Ministry
of Home Affairshas power to make grants by virtueof
sub-section(1) of thissection; and ,where the resolution
was passed by a county council,such determinationshall
not be arrivedatexceptupon the applicationofthecouncil
of the ruraldistrictwithin which the generalresolution
is in force .

SCHEDULE .
PART I.
General Adaptations .
Section 1 (3). (1) The enactments to which the severalParts of thisSchedule
hereinaftercontainedapply shallhave effect,in theirapplicationto
Northern Ireland,subjecttothe adaptationsand modificationssetout
in thisSchedule,save where inconsistentwith the provisionsof this
Act or the Government of IrelandAct ,1920,orany enactment amend-
ing the same .
(2) Subjectto the expressadaptationsand modificationsmade by
this Schedule, the General Adaptation of Enactments (Northern
Ireland) Order, 1921, and any other Order made by His Majesty in
CouncilundertheGovernmentofIrelandAct,1920,orany enactment
amending the same , containingadaptions of general application,
shall,ifand so far as they are applicableto the enactments adapted
by thisSchedule,apply theretoin likemanner as they apply to other
enactments .
(3) The adaptationsand modificationsmade by thisSchedule shall
apply to any order,scheme ,rule,regulationor instrument made or
issuedunder any ofthe enactments so adapted or modifiedand inforce
asrespectsNorthern Irelandimmediately beforethe appointedday ,in
likemanner as they apply to the enactment under which itwas made
orissued;and any suchorder,scheme,rule,regulationorinstrument
shallcontinueinforceas respectsNorthern Irelandinlikemanner and
subject to the likepowers of revocation and alterationas ifithad been
made or issuedunder the saidenactment as so adapted and modified.
2. Referencesin thisAct to any departmentof the Government
of the United Kingdom shallbe construedas includingreferencesto
theSecretaryofState,inany casewhere immediatelybeforetheappoin-
ted day the powers and dutiesof that department were,as respects
Northern Ireland,exerciseableby the Secretaryof Statein pursuance
of an Order of His Majesty in Council.

BEE itenacted by the King's most Excellent Majesty,

Northern Irelandor elsewhere) by any persons or body
of persons, being action of such a nature and on so
extensive a scale as to be calculated, by interfering
with the supply and distributionof food, water, fuel,

A proclamation of emergency shall continue in

againstany such regulationsshallbe imprisonment,

(NorthernIreland),1926.
CHAPTER 12 .
An Act to amend and extend the law relating to
ancient monuments , and to make provision for
the preservation of objects of archaeological
interest; and for other purposes in connection
therewith . [1st June , 1926.]
BE itenactedbytheKing'smostExcellentMajesty
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same , as follows:-
PART I.
GUARDIANSHIP OF ANCIENT MONUMENTS .
1.-(1) The owner of any monument which appears
to the Ministryof Finance to be an ancientmonument
within the meaning of thisAct may by deed appoint
thatMinistry,withitsconsent,guardianofthe monument .
(2) Where the owner of a monument appoints the
Ministry of Finance to be guardian of a monument ,
any person entitledto any estate or interestin the
monument ,whether such estateor interestisthe subject
of a settlementor not,may joinin the deed of appoint-
ment ,or may at any time afterthe executionofthe deed
of appointment execute a separatedeed,forthe purpose
ofmaking more effectivethe appointment ofthe Ministry
of Finance as guardian of the monument .
(3) Every such deed, to the extent to which it is
expressed to operate, and can operate, under thisAct ,
binds every person deriving titlefrom any person
executingit;and where the siteof a monument or any
estateor interestthereinisthe subjectof a settlement,
and a person executing the deed is a person having a
power of saleof the settledland, such deed binds every
person entitledto an estate,interestor charge subsisting
or to ariseunder the settlement,but subjectto,and with
the exception of,-
(i) an estate, interestor charge having priority
to the settlement ;

## Page 63

[16 & 17 GEO .5.] Ancient Monuments Act [Ch .12.] 57
(Northern Ireland),1926.
(ii) any estate,interestor charge which has been A.D.1926.
conveyed orcreatedforsecuringmoney actually
raised at the date of the deed ;
(iii) allleases, grants of easements or other rights
or privileges,granted or made beforethe date
of the deed by the person executingthe deed
or by any of hispredecessorsintitleor by any
trustees for him or them under the settlement
or under any statutory power, or being
otherwise binding on the successorsof the
person executingthe deed.
(4) For the purposes of this Act the expression
" owner ," where used in relationto a monument ,means
any person entitledto any estateor interestin the site
ofthe monument who ,by virtueofsuch estateorinterest,
isentitledto the actualpossessionofthe monument ,and
includesany body corporate,localauthority,corporation,
trustees for charities, or commissioners or trustees for
ecclesiastical, collegiateor other public purposes.
(5) Except as providedby thisAct,the righttothe
possession of a monument or lands adjoiningthereto
shallnot be affectedby theappointmentoftheMinistry
of Finance as guardian under thisAct.
2.-(1) Where the Ministryof Finance has been
appointed guardian of any monument under thisAct ,
that Ministry shallmaintain the monument and shall
have accessby itsinspectors, agents or workmen to the
monument for the purposes of inspectingit and of
bringingsuch materialsand doing such acts and things
as may be requiredfor itsmaintenance :
Provided that,ifa person who isnot bound by the
deed by which the Ministry of Finance was appointed
guardian becomes owner of the monument , the power
of that Ministry to maintain the monument may be
determined by noticein writingsigned by such person
and served on that Ministry, and such notice shall
operate from the date of the servicethereof.
(2) The expression“ maintenance " in thissection
includes the fencing, repairingand covering in of a
monument and the doing of any otheract or thingwhich
may be requiredfor the purpose of repairingthe monu-
ment or protectingit from decay or injury, and the
expression " maintain " shallbe construed accordingly.
Effectof
ship.
guardian .

PART II .
ACQUISITION OF ANCIENT MONUMENTS .
3. The Ministry of Finance may purchase by
agreement any monument which appears to itto be an
ancient monument within the meaning of thisAct .
4. Any person may ,by deed or will,give,deviseor
bequeath to the MinistryofFinance the estateor interest
in any ancientmonument of which he may be seisedor
possessed, and that Ministrymay accept any such gift,
devise or bequest if, in the opinion of that Ministry, it
isexpedient to do so.
PART III .
PROTECTION OF ANCIENT MONUMENTS .
5.-(1) The Ministryof Finance shallfrom time to
time cause to be prepared and published a listor lists
containing-
(a) such monuments as are reported by the
Advisory Committee constitutedunder this
Act (in thisAct referredto as " the Ancient
Monuments Advisory Committee " ) as being
ancient monuments the preservation of which
isof nationalimportance ; and
(b) such otherancientmonuments as the Ministry
of Finance thinks fit;
and that Ministryshall, when itisintended to include
a monument inthelist,notifythe owner ofthe monument
of such intentionand of the penaltieswhich may be
incurredby a person guiltyof an offenceunder the next
succeeding sub -section.
(2) Where the owner of any ancient monument
which is included in any such listof monuments as
aforesaid, afterbeing notifiedas provided in the last
preceding sub-section, proposes to demolish or removein whole or in part, alter structurally, or make
additionsto,the monument ,or make excavationsin the
neighbourhood thereof, he shallforthwith give notice
ofhisintentionto the Ministryof Finance,and shallnot,
except in the case of urgent necessity, commence any
work of demolition, removal, alteration, addition or
excavation,fora periodoftwo months afterhaving given

## Page 65

[16 & 17 GEO .5.] AncientMonuments Act 59[Ch .12.]
(Northern Ireland), 1926 .
such notice; and any person guiltyof a contravention
of or non -compliance with thisprovisionshallbe liable,
on convictionunder the Summary Jurisdiction(Ireland)
Acts,to a finenot exceeding one hundred pounds ,or to
imprisonment for a term not exceeding three months ,
or to both .
6. (1) If the Ancient Monuments Advisory Com-
mittee reportto the Ministryof Finance that any monu-
ment isin danger of destructionor removal or damage
from neglect or injudicioustreatment, and that the
preservationof the monument isof nationalimportance,
the Ministry of Finance may , if it appears that the
monument is an ancient monument within the meaning
of thisAct, make an order (in thisAct referredto as a
PreservationOrder) placing the monument under the
protectionof that Ministry:
Provided that,ifinany casethe MinistryofFinance
considersthat the making of such an order isa matter
of immediate urgency, the order may be made without
receivingany such report as aforesaid.
(2) Where the Ancient Monuments Advisory Com-
mittee have reason to believethat any monument isin
danger as aforesaid, and that the preservationof the
monument is of nationalimportance, they may them-
selves,or by any person authorisedin writingby them ,
enterat any reasonabletime upon any premisesforthe
purpose of enablingthem to determineby inspection
of the monument whether itisproper forthem to report
to the Ministryof Finance :
Provided that, unless the Ancient Monuments
Advisory Committee considerthat the inspectionof the
monument isa matter of immediate urgency,they shall
give not lessthan seven cleardays'noticeto the occupier
of the premisesoftheirintentionso to enterupon them .
(3) Every PreservationOrder shallbe laid before
both Houses of Parliament as soon as may be afteritis
made ,and ifeitherof thoseHouses withinthe statutory
periodnext afterany PreservationOrder islaidbeforeit
by resolutionannuls the same , such PreservationOrder
shallforthwithbecome void, but without prejudiceto
the validityofanything which in the meantime may have
been done thereunder. Subject as aforesaid,a Preserva-
tionOrder shallhave effectuntilrevoked by the Ministry
of Finance .

For the purpose of thissub-sectionthe expression
" statutoryperiod" means a periodcomprisingfivedays
at leaston which the House in questionhas sat,but not
being in any case shorterin duration than ten days ,
and days comprised in more than one sessionof Parlia-
ment may be reckoned for that purpose.
7.-(1) While a PreservationOrder isin force,the
monument to which the Order relates shall not be de-
molished or removed , nor shallany additionsor altera-
tionsbe made theretoor any work be carriedout in con-
nectiontherewith,except with the writtenconsentof the
Ministry of Finance.
(2) If, while a PreservationOrder is in force, it
appears to the Ministryof Finance that, owing to the
neglect of the owner or person having control of the
monument ,the monument isliableto fallintodecay,the
Ministryof Finance may make an Order appointingthat
Ministryguardian ofthe monument forthe periodduring
which the Preservation Order isin force,and in that case
the provisionsof thisAct shall,during that period,take
effectas ifthe Ministryof Finance had been appointed
guardian by virtueof a deed executed by every person
seisedor possessedof,or entitledto,an estateor interest
in the monument .
(3) Any ordermade under the lastprecedingsub-
sectionmay be revoked at any time by the Ministry of
Finance .
8. If any person injuresor defacesany monument
of which the Ministryof Finance or a county councilis
the owner or guardian, or which is the subject of a
Preservation Order , or which has been included in a list
of monuments published by the Ministry of Finance
under thisPart ofthisAct,thatpersonshall,on conviction
under the Summary Jurisdiction(Ireland) Acts, be
liableto a finenot exceedingfivepounds,and ,in addition
to the fine,to pay such sums as the courtby whom he
istriedthinkjustforthe purposeofrepairingany damages
caused by him , or to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding one month .
9.-(1) Where,under the powers conferredby this
Act , any act isdone involvinginterferencewith private
rightsof property,compensation shallbe payable by the
Ministry of Finance.

(NorthernIreland), 1926.
(2) If any dispute arisesas to the amount of such
compensation, such question shallbe referredto, and
determined by,an officialarbitratorunder theAcquisition
of Land (Assessment of Compensation) Act , 1919, and
sectionsthreeand sixofthat Act shallapply accordingly.

GENERAL .

thereof .

Ministry by virtueof a PreservationOrder.
(2) The Ministryof Finance may superintendany
work inconnectionwith any ancientmonument ifinvited
to do so by the owner, and shallsuperintendany such
work ,whether requiredto do so by the owner or not,in
connection with any monument which is placed under
theirprotectionby virtueof a PreservationOrder.
(3) Any such advice and superintendenceshallbe
given and affordedfreeof charge,except that a charge
may be made for out-of-pocket expenses in the case of
monuments which have not been placed under the
protectionof the Ministry of Finance by virtue of a
Preservation Order .

17. In this Act the expression “ monument
includesany site, structureor erection(whether above
or below the surface)otherthan an ecclesiasticalbuilding
which is for the time being used for ecclesiastical
purposes; and the expression " ancient monumentincludes any monument or part or remains of
monument , the preservationof which is a matter of
public interestby reason of the historic, architectural,
traditional, artistic, or archaeologicalinterestattaching
thereto, and the siteof any such monument or of any
remains thereof, and any part of the adjoining land
which may be requiredforthe purposeoffencing,covering
in, or otherwisepreservingthe monument from injury,
or for the purpose of preservingthe amenities of the
monument ,and alsoincludes the means of accessthereto.
18.- (1) The finder of any archaeologicalobject
shall, within fourteen days of such finding, report the
findingand characterofthe objectand the circumstances
of the finding to the Ancient Monuments Advisory
Committee .
(2) Any person,beinga finderofan archaeological
object, who without reasonablecause failsto reportthe
findingof such objectas provided by sub-section(1) of
thissectionor who refusesto give informationor gives
falseinformationof the characterof the objectfound,
or of the circumstances of the finding, to the Ancient
Monuments Advisory Committee or to such person or
personsas may be prescribedby the Ministryof Finance
shallbe liable,on convictionunder the Summary Juris-
diction(Ireland)Acts,to a finenot exceedingfivepounds ,
or to imprisonment fora term not exceedingone month .
ود
(3) In thissectionthe expression“ archaeological
object means any object,being a chattelwhether in amanufactured or unmanufactured state, which, by
reason of its archaeologicalor historicinterest, has a
valuesubstantiallygreaterthan itsintrinsicvalue or the
value of the materialsof which itis composed .

3. The followingprovisionsshallhave effectin lieu
of the provisionscontained in sectiontwenty of the
JuriesProcedure (Ireland)Act ,1876 (in thisAct referred
to as " the JuriesProcedure Act "),that isto say :-

to thisAct shallbe absolutelyfreedand exempted
from being returnedand from servingon any jury,

exemption when it firstarises) or in any jurors
books :
Provided that no verdict or trial shall be
invalid or impeached on the ground that any
person so exempted was sworn and served upon
the jury which found such verdictat such trial.

13.-(1) For the purpose of releasingjurorsfrom
attendance for any period during the sittingof a court
when theyarenotimmediatelyrequired,thejudgeofany ofjurors.
court may , if he thinks fit, divide into two or more
sectionsany panel ofjurorsreturnedto thatcourtby the
sheriff; and the powers of such judge shallbe extended
so as to enable him to excuse from attendance on any
specifieddays during the sittingof the court allof the
jurorswhose names appear in any one or more of the
sectionsinto which the panel has been divided.
(2) It ishereby declaredthatthe powers of a judge
includea power , at the conclusionof a trialof an ex-
ceptionallyexacting nature, to excuse the members of
the jury on such trialfrom furtherjury service,forsuch
period as the judge may think fit.

relatesshallbe quashed,stayed or reversedbecause,by
reason only of the provisionsof this section, the body
was not viewed by the jury upon an inquest.

Act .

ofthe Act of 1879 shallretirecompulsorilybeforeattain-

CHAPTER 17 .
An Act to amend the Firearms Act , 1920 ,in its
application to Northern Ireland .
BE
[1st June , 1926.]
E it enacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same , as follows:---
1.-(1) No offenceunder sectionone of the Fire-
arms Act,1920 (in thisAct referredto as " the principal
Act " ) shall be deemed to be committed in the case of
any person, by having in his possessionwithin his

## Page 113

[16 & 17 GEO .5.] Firearms (Amendment )Act [Ch .17.] 107
(Northern Ireland), 1926 .
A.D. 1926 .
offirearms,
dwelling-house a firearm or ammunition therefor, pro-
vided that he has obtained a permit for that purpose destruction
underthissection(inthisAct referredto as a " firearm
permit"); and sub-section (8) of section one of the
principalAct shallhave effectaccordingly.
(2) A chiefofficerof policehaving power to grant
firearmcertificatesunder the principalAct shallhave
power to grant a firearm permit to any person in his
districtwho appliesforsuchpermit,ifhe issatisfiedthat
the applicantisa person who can,without danger to the
publicsafetyor to the peace, be permitted to have in
his possessionwithin his dwelling-house a firearm and
ammunition therefor, and on payment of the prescribed
fee .
(3) A firearm permit shall be in the prescribed
form, and shallspecifythe arms and ammunition in
respectof which itisissued,and shall,unlesspreviously
revoked or cancelled,continuein forceforone year,but
shallbe renewablefora furtherperiodof one year by the
chiefofficerof policeof the districtin which the holder
of the permit resides,and so from time to time. A fire-
arm permit may be revoked by such chiefofficerofpolice
ifhe issatisfiedthat the holderof the permit isunfitted
to have possessionof a firearmor ammunition .
(4) The followingfees shallbe paid on the grant
and renewal, respectively, of a firearmpermit :-
Where the applicantisnot the holderof a firearm
permit at the time of the application- Two
shillingsand sixpence;
Where the applicantisthe holderofa firearmpermit
in forceat the time of the applicationand is
applying for the renewal of the permit- One
shilling.
(5) A chiefofficerof policemay order that any
firearm (other than firearmsto which sectionthirteen
of the principalAct applies) or ammunition, which is
surrenderedto, or seizedor found by any policeofficer
orconstable,and inrespectofwhich a firearmpermitor
a firearmcertificateor a permit under the principalAct
has not been granted, shallbe destroyedor otherwise
disposed of.

CHAPTER 20 .
An Act to continue certain Expiring Laws as
respects Northern Ireland .
[30th November , 1926.]
WHEREAS theActs(whetherpassedbytheParlia-of the United Kingdom or by the
Parliament of Northern Ireland) mentioned in the
Schedule to thisAct are,in so faras they are in forcein
Northern Irelandand are temporary in theirduration,
limitedto expire on the thirty-firstday ofDecember ,
nineteenhundred and twenty-six:
And whereasitisexpedientto provideforthe continuance
as in thisAct mentioned of those Acts , and of the enact-
ments amending or affectingthe same :
Be it thereforeenacted by the King's most Excellent
Majesty, and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same , as follows:-

## Page 117

[16 & 17 GEO .5.] Expiring Laws Continuance [Ch .20.] 111
Act (Northern Ireland), 1926.
1.- (1) The Acts mentioned in the severalParts of
the Schedule to thisAct shall,to the extent specifiedin
column threeof that Schedule, be continued as respects
Northern Irelanduntilthe thirty-firstday of December ,
nineteen hundred and twenty-seven, and shall then
expire unless further continued.
(2) Any unrepealedenactments amending or affect-
ing the enactments continuedby thisAct shall,in so far
as they are temporary in theirduration, be continued in
likemanner ,whether they arementioned inthe Schedule
to this Act or not .
2.-(1) ThisAct may be citedas the Expiring Laws
Continuance Act (Northern Ireland), 1926.
(2) Referencesin thisAct to any enactments ofthe
Parliament of the United Kingdom shallbe construedas
referencesto thoseenactments as they apply in Northern
Ireland .
(3) Nothing inthisAct shallbe construedas affect-
ing any enactment in so faras the enactment relatesto a
matter with respectto which the Parliament ofNorthern
Irelandhas not power to make laws.

CHAPTER 21 .
An Act to amend section eleven of the Industrial
Assurance Act (Northern Ireland), 1924 , with
respect to the exemption from that Act of
juvenile societies. [30th November , 1926.]
B E itenacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same , as follows:-
1. For section eleven of the Industrial Assurance
Act (Northern Ireland), 1924,the followingsectionshall
be substituted :--
" 11.-(1) ThisAct shallnot apply to a juvenile
societywithin the meaning ofthissectionnotwithstanding
that premiums ofthe juvenilemembers ofthe societyare
receivedby means of collectors, if and so long as no
premiums of any members of the societywho are not
juvenilemembers are so received.
" (2) For the purposesofthissectionthe expression
'juvenilesociety' means a friendlysocietyor branch ,
registeredin Great Britain or Northern Ireland,which
consistswholly or in part of juvenilemembers , and
which is shown to the satisfaction of the Commissioner
to be connectedwith,or isa branch of,a friendlysociety
so registeredbefore the firstday of July, nineteen
hundred and twenty -six; and the expression‘juvenile
member ' means a member under the age of eighteen
years."
2. ThisAct may be citedastheIndustrialAssurance
(Juvenile Societies) Act (Northern Ireland), 1926, and
shall be construed as one with the Industrial Assurance
Act (Northern Ireland),1924,and that Act and thisAct
may be citedtogetheras the IndustrialAssurance Acts
(Northern Ireland), 1924 and 1926.

CHAPTER 22 .
An Act to confirm and give effectto an agreement
relating to the transfer of the Malone Training
School to the Ministry of Home Affairsforthe
purposes ofa Reformatory School and a Borstal
Institution, and for purposes connected there-
with . [30th November , 1926.]
Way ofMayamagreementdatedthesentent
HEREAS by an agreement dated the seventeenth
made between William Augustus Ferrar, solesurviving
trusteeforand on behalfofthe Societycalledthe MaloneProtestantReformatory (in thisAct referredto as " the
trustee")of the firstpart,John A. Rankin ,Joshua Pim ,

Crossley, the Reverend S. R. McGarvey , the Reverend
J. G. Paton , William Bruce Rainey Joy , ColonelJames
Morwood , James G. Marks ,and John Maynard Sinclair,
being the Committee of Management of the saidSociety
(in thisAct referredto as " the committee of manage-
ment ") of the second part, and the Ministryof Home
Affairsfor Northern Ireland (in thisAct referredto as
" the Ministryof Home Affairs") of the third part,
which agreement isset out in the Schedule to thisAct ,
and isin thisAct referredto as " the agreement," itwas
agreed that,subjectto the obtainingof the authorityof
the Ministry of Finance, so far as such authority is
required under the enactments in force in Northern
Ireland with respectto charitabledonations and bequests,
and tothe passingofan Act ofthe ParliamentofNorthern
Irelandforgivingeffecttothe agreement,and to the other
conditions mentioned therein, the Ministry of Home
Affairs should take over from the trustee and the com-
mittee of management the premises described in the
agreement,beingthe premisesofthe Reformatory School
calledthe Malone Training School, and should use the
saidpremises for the purposes of a Reformatory School
and a Borstal Institution for Northern Ireland :
And whereas the authority of the Ministry of
Finance,sofarasrequiredunder the enactments aforesaid,
has been obtained :
And whereas the provisions of the agreement
cannot take effectwithout the authorityof Parliament :
A.D. 1926 .

Ireland,and known as the Societyof the Inn of Court ofNorthern Ireland (in this sectionreferredto as " the
Society" )has been formed forthe purpose(amongst other
purposes)ofregulatingadmissiontothe Bar and providing
for the legaleducationof studentsin Northern Ireland,
and it is expedient that contributionsshould be made
towards the expensesofthe Societyout ofthe proceedsof
the stamp dutiespayableby studentson admissionto the
Society,and on calltothe Bar ofNorthern Ireland:
Therefore,the MinistryofFinance shallpay to the
treasurerof the Society, to be appliedby him accord-
ingto the directionsofthe Society,the followingsums out
of, or consistingof, the duties paid in each financial

of barrister-at-law in Northern Irelandand upon every
admission of a person to be a student of the Society(which dutiesare in thissub-sectionreferredto as " the
admissionduties"),that isto say :-

CHAPTER 26 .
An Act to remove doubts as to the powers oflocal
authoritiesto make certain payments for the
purposes ofsectionone ofthe Local Government
(Emergency Provisions) Act, 1916.
BE
[30th November , 1926 ].
E it enacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityofthe same ,asfollows:--
1.- (1) In calculatingthe amount of any payment
or payments , based on salary or wages, which a local
authorityat any time during the latewar agreedto make ,
for any purpose authorisedby sectionone of the Local
Government (Emergency Provisions) Act, 1916, to an
officerorservantto whom the saidsectionwas applicable,
or to the wife, widow or other dependants of any such
officeror servant,the localauthoritymay ,ifthey think
fit,take intoaccount any bonus and increment of salary
or wages which would have been payable to such officer
or servant,ifhe had remained in the actual serviceof the

## Page 141

[16 & 17 GEO .5.] Local Government 135[Ch . 26,27.]
(War ServicePayments ) Act
(NorthernIreland), 1926.
localauthorityduringtheperiodofhisserviceinorwith
HisMajesty'sForces(includingserviceinconnectionwith
naval or militaryoperationsto which the saidsection

pay,or agreeto pay ,such proportion(ifany ) of the said
bonus and increment of salary or wages as they may
decide,but in no case exceedingthe proportionof salary
or wages specifiedin any agreement made beforethe
termination of the late war .
(2) Notwithstandingany enactment tothecontrary,
payments made under thisAct shallbe deemed to be
lawfullymade if made beforethe thirty-firstday of
March ,nineteenhundred and twenty-eight;and payments
made at any time beforethe passingof thisAct shallbe
deemed to have been lawfullymade ,ifand so faras they
would have been authorisedby thisAct had itbeen
then in force .

(a) the premises of any person engaged in the
businessof carryinggoods forreward ;
(b) any pier, quay, wharf, jetty, dock or dock
premises; and
(c) any ship, boat, railwaywaggon, motor lorry,
cart or other vessel or vehicle used for the
conveyance of goods ;
and to open, for the purpose of examination, cases of
eggs marked in accordance with the rulesfor the time
being prescribedby the Ministry,and caseswhich he has
reason to believeought to be so marked , which may be
found in or upon any premises, vesselor vehiclewhich
he is entitled to enter under this section .
(2) Where any caseofeggsisexamined by an officer
under thissection,the caseshallbe marked by the officer
to that effect; and such mark shall be deemed to be a
sufficientnotificationto the consignee that the case
has been so examined , and the Ministryshallnotifythe
consignor of the examination .
9.-(1) ThisAct may be citedas the Marketingof
Eggs Act (Northern Ireland),1926,and shallbe construed
as one with the principalAct,and that Act and thisAct
may be citedtogether as the Marketing of Eggs Acts
(Northern Ireland), 1924 and 1926.
(2) This Act shall come into operation on the
firstday ofJanuary ,nineteenhundred and twenty -seven.

of an offence under this Act .
